    <li> I am a light skinned, brunette. I&#x27;ve had a mustache since I was 8 years old.. so needless to say my battle against my facial hair started early. I have literally tried it all. I have tried it all, with varying results.. but this tool has change everything!!    You do not have to be in front of a mirror, or near an outlet! I pick it up while I&#x27;m watching TV and go over my trouble areas.. or right before I wash my face at night. I use it everyday and I no longer have those inbetween waxing days where I feel less confident, my face is always hair free and smooth now. Now, I do have fast regrowth so someone less hairy might not have to use it ever day, but if you have to, this is the tool to do it. You don&#x27;t necessarily have to bend the spring into a tight U shape as shown in the pictures (you can also use it bent just a little into a wide rounded U shape).&lt;br /&gt;2.) Lay the spring against your skin just below where you want to remove the hair.&lt;br /&gt;3.) As you slowly move the spring upward, twirl the right hand fingers clockwise and the left hand fingers counter-clockwise. If you twirl them the opposite way, no hairs get grabbed (this was the main thing I needed to figure out and the instructions didn&#x27;t explain it).&lt;br /&gt;4.) Doing this grips the hairs and pulls them out, and yes, it does hurt for a split second but no longer than that and it doesn&#x27;t leave your skin at all pink or red or irritated.  I suspect it hurts more when you first start using it, but after multiple uses, I&#x27;m thinking it will hurt less.&lt;br /&gt;I cannot understand why the REM company doesn&#x27;t explain how important it is to twirl your fingers in the right direction.  I was ready to toss the thing. I should add that the hairs I want to grip are not at all unusual (just your average thing). So I&#x27;m giving this 4 stars instead of 5 only because I had to figure this out for myself, whereas the company could have done a better job of explaining how to use it. Once you figure this stuff out, the spring itself does a great job and is worth 5 stars for how it actually works.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Update: I have used this for quite a while now, and it by far hurts the most the first time you use it, I guess because it is grabbing the most hairs that first time.  I find that I need to use it 2 or 3 times a week, and when you do that, you&#x27;re only picking up those hairs that are long enough to be grabbed.  It hurts much less because there are less hairs than the first time (I think individual hairs grow at different rates).  So definitely do not judge this based on the first-time level of pain - it&#x27;s no big deal and I LOVE the way it works.  I have read what other people said about turning \\&quot;both hands in, then both hands out\\&quot; and that accomplishes the same thing I recommended (right hand clockwise, left hand counterclockwise) - that accomplishes \\&quot;both hands in\\&quot; and that is the sweep that grabs the hairs and pulls them out. The \\&quot;both hands out\\&quot; doesn&#x27;t grab any hairs.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Another update:  I&#x27;m still using this 2-3 times a week and I love it!  I have noticed one additional thing that I thought I would mention.  I have a magnifying mirror which I use occasionally and I&#x27;ve noticed that there are a few hairs that grow in somewhat different directions from the others.  Most of my hairs get grabbed when I sweep upwards at them from below, but there are a few that grow in an upward direction, or from right to left or left to right, and those weren&#x27;t getting grabbed with the others.  So now I sweep at the hairs from every possible direction: upwards, downwards, right to left, left to right, diagonally, etc.  This picks up those remaining hairs.  This also should help if you&#x27;re trying to get hairs on a curvy surface like your chin area. Just remember that whatever direction you&#x27;re sweeping, the right hand goes clockwise and the left hand goes counter clockwise.you&#x27;re only picking up those hairs that are long enough to be grabbed.  It hurts much less because there are less hairs than the first time (I think individual hairs grow at different rates).  So definitely do not judge this based on the first-time level of pain - it&#x27;s no big deal and I LOVE the way it works.  I have read what other people said about turning \\&quot;both hands in, then both hands out\\&quot; and that accomplishes the same thing I recommended (right hand clockwise, left hand counterclockwise) - that accomplishes \\&quot;both hands in\\&quot; and that is the sweep that grabs the hairs and pulls them out. The \\&quot;both hands out\\&quot; doesn&#x27;t grab any hairs.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Another update:  I&#x27;m still using this 2-3 times a week and I love it!  I have noticed one additional thing that I thought I would mention.  I have a magnifying mirror which I use occasionally and I&#x27;ve noticed that there are a few hairs that grow in somewhat different directions from the others.  Most of my hairs get grabbed when I sweep upwards at them from below, but there are a few that grow in an upward direction, or from right to left or left to right, and those weren&#x27;t getting grabbed with the others.  So now I sweep at the hairs from every possible direction: upwards, downwards, right to left, left to right, diagonally, etc.  This picks up those remaining hairs.  This also should help if you&#x27;re trying to get hairs on a curvy surface like your chin area. Just remember that whatever direction you&#x27;re sweeping, the right hand goes clockwise and the left hand goes counter clockwise.</li>

    <li> This product works amazingly well but requires some practice.  The most important thing to know is that you must approach the hair from opposite the direction of growth. And it doesn&#x27;t come out of carpet!)&lt;br /&gt;-Went from the 30 min- heat, apply, wait...wait....wait...RIP, clean up&lt;br /&gt;TO:&lt;br /&gt;-Run spring over lips quickly to numb &amp; then finish off the rest in about 5 minutes or less&lt;br /&gt;-I get cold sores and I have a TON less irritation after using this than I ever did with wax!&lt;br /&gt;-It is a tad embarrassing, but yes I do get chin hairs &amp; the spring works great on that area as well&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I originally stumbled on this product when I had a cold sore, and wanted to use something more gentle.  I did some research, and saw a YouTube video on this (At first I thought OMG! That looks terrible-  TRUST me, its not!)  So it is a spring with two handles on each end.  You will NEVER pinch your skin, so don&#x27;t worry about that! When I run it over my lips to help numb; I hold the spring horizontal and then really quickly roll it down &amp; out(away from you).  You&#x27;ll start by holding it with your thumb &amp; your index finger.  Your thumb will be closer to your face--- As you roll (down/back &amp; out) your index finger will come closer to your face &amp; thumb will move downward &amp; away)  I just keep doing this until I notice that it is not painful anymore and then begin with more detail.  When you begin in more detail you can place the spring in multiple directions (not all of the hair &amp;#34;lays&amp;#34; the same way- think of this as &amp;#34;going against the grain&amp;#34; some hair is easier to remove at a different angle than the rest.  I usually start at one corner of my mouth or &amp;#34;st-ache&amp;#34; area: Place the spring to &amp;#34;follow&amp;#34; your lips shape and then roll UP.  You will know when you are at a good angle because you can feel it grabbing more hair (not in a painful way, but a &amp;#34;hey its grabbing a lot&amp;#34; kind of way)  then I work toward the center.  The middle usually does hurt a little more, so I typically go up to where my upper lips &amp;#34;points&amp;#34; are, and then Ill start at the other outer st-ache corner area on the opposite side of my mouth.  Then when I&#x27;ve worked my way in, and its pretty much all numb, I will place the spring over my entire top lip lining and roll up to get the middle hairs.  It is much easier to experiment &amp; see what works best for you.  But don&#x27;t be intimidated, it is much faster, less messy, and less painful because you sort of ease the pain in which allows your skin to adjust instead of one big RIP and that tingly/irritated feeling after you wax.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Good luck!  Watch the youtube videos if you are still unsure of how to use this product, it helped me in the beginning!&lt;br /&gt;Don&#x27;t think that it is complicated, it is just hard to explain if I am not showing you how</li>

    <li> I wonder why so many people are unhappy with the R.E.M. spring.  I have been using it for many months to happily (if sometimes painfully) rip out the hairs on my upper lip.  I twist the spring against my skin so I feel it catch the hairs I want removed, adjust if necessary, and pull.  Of course, it took some experimentation to learn the proper technique.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I suspect many users&#x27; difficulty lies in following the official directions too closely.  Those never did me any good, and the motion was exhausting to repeat as much as I needed to do it.  The motions I use to catch hair in the spring are small, subtle, and effortless.  It&#x27;s more bending than twisting the item; gently separating the coils of the spring, applying it to the roots of the unwanted hair, closing the coils over them, and commencing a pulling and rolling motion.  It is very quick.  It helps to go against the growth direction of the offending hairs, and you might even want to ruffle them so they&#x27;re standing up before you apply the spring.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Voila: you may now elegantly decimate your moustache, or whatever.  (Please do not get this thing anywhere near your eyebrows, though.)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;As for pain--yes, it does hurt if I&#x27;ve left the mini-moustache to grow for a few weeks. Your experience may vary, of course.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I find that it helps to shower, or at least wash my face, in very warm water if I&#x27;m having difficulty.     <li> We all know that Michael &amp; co haven&#x27;t particularly been cranking out new material in the last decade or two; but in the good old days, artists could at least fall back on existing album sales for a decent retirement. Every once in a while, when the itch to \\&quot;live large\\&quot; needs a scratch, hey, get the band back together and hit the road for another \\&quot;greatest hits\\&quot; tour, supporting another \\&quot;greatest hits\\&quot; album.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Well, all was fine and good until digital media upset the Apple cart. Now with the kids sharing their Bit-Torrent files across the web in their iTunes programs, nobody&#x27;s selling units anymore. And every pimply teen with an iPad has every greatest hits compilation you could ever make. Now the only time the gravy train rolls into the station for elderly and burned out artists is a new tour. Watching these codgers drag themselves across the stage at your local highly-flammible nightclub borders on the inhumane. Instead of treasuring the music of your childhood, now you have to see it fumbled out from the arthritic fingers of your idols of yesteryear.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This is all to give a little background to the sad story of REM and their latest merchandising play. While branching out like this is an ingenious way to avoid leaving the house (getting prescription refills for your hypertension and high cholesterol is such a pain on tour! And forget about dealing with the insurance coverage), I have to say that branding a nose hair remover with the previously solid \\&quot;Alternative\\&quot; brand of REM might have been a mis-step. I am sure that the band members love the product (when you get old, hair comes out of your nose, ears and other unexpected holes) but maybe they could have held out for a classier product- I mean, even that rapist Vince guy has the Slap Chop.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Anyway, I&#x27;m sure the REM Nose Hair Pulling Spring is great; but don&#x27;t expect it to bring you back to the magic teen years like listening to \\&quot;Document\\&quot; does.</li>

If it hurts and you want to chicken out before ripping your hairs out, roll them in the opposite direction (for example, if turning away from your face pulls, turn toward your face to release).  Pull your skin taut to prevent excessive tugging on the skin.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;5.  After effects? I&#x27;m sticking with my electric razor.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you have thin women&#x27;s hair, this may be different.
